[{"Title":"Not just a silly slasher film","Date":"7 March 2005","Score":"64 out of 89 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" A group of model-caliber San Francisco women who have been friends since elementary school are suddenly being threatened and attacked by someone sending them bizarre Valentine's Day cards. Who is the killer and why is the killer after them? My rating will often change on subsequent viewings of a film--sometimes slightly up, sometimes slightly down. However, I can't remember another film where my rating has changed as drastically as it has for Valentine. The first time I watched it, upon its theatrical release, I thought it was pretty awful--I gave it a 4 out of 10, the equivalent of an F letter grade. Watching it for a second time last night, I can't remember what the heck I didn't like about it. I can only assume that maybe I was really in the wrong mood to watch it, or maybe I just didn't get it. In any event, I loved it this time, giving it a 9 out of 10, or an A.It might sound ridiculous saying I didn't get a film like this, but there is something to get. Valentine is almost a comedy/horror. Director Jamie Blanks, who was also responsible for 1998's Urban Legend, takes the stereotypical teen horror formula that became so popular in the late 1990s in the wake of Scream (1996) and pushes most of the elements up a notch, making Valentine intentionally cheesy/campy almost to the point of absurdity (where absurdism is a positive stylistic term). On top of that, he gives us a film imbued with humorous commentary on romantic relationships. The humor is unusual in that it has the same exaggeratedly campy tone as the teen horror aspects. Most of the situations in the film, and the modus operandi of the villain, humorous or not, are tied in to the Valentine's Day theme.Many viewers will likely subtract points from the film for its various cliché-rooted but implausible scenarios and plot developments. However, in light of the above, the film is intentionally clichéd, implausible and ludicrous. It's as if Blanks is attempting (and mostly succeeding) to transcend the typical teen slasher by mocking/spoofing the conventions of the genre while also satirizing eros. That's the attraction to the irony of basing a horror film on Valentine's Day. It's an incongruity that is cleverly woven throughout the film, and that is itself at the heart of the slasher genre, making it prime fodder for Valentine's extravagant lampooning. Scream had a similar aim with its horror material, but the twist there was that the film was self-aware. Valentine's Day is intentionally not self-aware; the viewer has to rely on contextual clues for satire. Lest some think I'm reading too much into the film, it's worthwhile to note that Blanks said in interviews that he didn't want to just do another slasher film after Urban Legend and producer Dylan Sellers said he wanted to do something more adult.Other viewers may dislike the fact that Valentine's Day differs so much from its putative source material, the novel of the same name by Tom Savage. The novel's characters, setting and plot are very different from the film. Sellers has said, While it was a fine book, I didn't think it was the right story for a film. So instead the novel, which is much dryer and more serious in tone, was used as a launching pad, a motif to create variations on for a horror/thriller story centered on Valentine's Day. While those facts won't help purists familiar with the book like the film, it's helpful to understand why the film has its divergent plot and attitude. It's probably better to look at the film as an independent entity with a similar theme.Blanks' direction is impeccable visually. Valentine's Day has a lush look throughout, with complex, deep colors, interesting sets, and good staging. Blanks is admirable for keeping his villain and attack scenes not too dark, with clearly conveyed action. He also directs his actors with aplomb, catalyzing often slyly humorous performances. David Boreanaz, as Adam Carr, is involved in many of the funniest moments.While Valentine's Day is no masterpiece, it's a very good horror/thriller film that seems strongly prone to misconceptions. If you watch it expecting something more tongue-in-cheek you may find yourself appreciating it a lot more. "},{"Title":"A great slasher with a very misleading rating","Date":"28 March 2008","Score":"24 out of 33 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" I wanted to see Valentine ever since I saw that Denise Richards and Marley Shelton starred in it, because they had played in some of my favorite movies ever and some of the most enjoyable films, or so I thought, released in recent years. When I actually watched Valentine, I was amazed at how great the story line actually was for a slasher flick, and even though it has problems as any other slasher does, it is really entertaining and fun from beginning to end, which is all I need from a slasher to be satisfied.It pains me to see that it has a low rating, because it was not that horrible at all. The actors and actresses played the parts wonderfully, or at least to the best of their ability with the characters and screenplay that they were given, and the way it ended was so brilliant and cunning, even if many don't think so, or were already put off at that point. Some scenes were a little unbelievable and/or poor, and I confess at a few minor parts it got just a bit boring, but overall it was non-stop entertaining and actually suspenseful, the first time around at least. It had a mind-twisting story line which made you guess the whole way through, as do most slasher movies, and it doesn't deserve all the crap it gets. I recommend this movie to watch anytime, but especially on Valentine's Day because it's sure to give you a ton of chills. Oh, and don't even pay attention to the trailer or rating. One of those films was the 1981 Canadian made My Bloody Valentine, which I hated alot. Valentine is a better film than that one, but it's not saying much. The plot a nerdy young boy is teased and pranked by a couple of his classmates at the beginning of the film. Then the film moves years later when those classmates are all grown up, then they're picked off one-by-one. The killer is presumed to be the young boy now all grown up looking for revenge. "},{"Title":"It's no Citizen Kane, but great for the genre","Date":"2 February 2001","Score":"1 out of 1 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  Jamie Blanks' Valentine is a stylish horror flick that hearkens more to Halloween than to his idiotic other film, Urban Legends. Some may say comparing this film to Halloween is a disservice to that brilliant movie, but I was thoroughly entertained by Valentine and think that most people will be. For fans of wonderfully visual films like The Cell and Seven, as I am, it will be even better of an experience. Horror films are not the place for those looking for psychological tension. The current breed of these films are cold, dark and nihilistic, and this is definitely one of the best of those. Look at the amazing way Blanks captures the killer in the film's first scene, with swinging lamps and dark corridors, the slash of his knife pounding into corpses with deafening thuds. Or his Cupid's arrows ripping into one of his victims. For those looking for a thinking movie, look elsewhere. But for horror fans or those just looking for some really cool cinematography, Valentine is definitely worth your while. "},{"Title":"giallo, American style","Date":"5 January 2007","Score":"2 out of 3 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" Face it slasher films are not art. They're cheap, nasty, ugly, vulgar, despicable, misogynistic exploitation pics that appeal to the basest, most primitive instinct of our collective id. That's not to say I don't enjoy them, but I have no illusions about their ultimate worth. When you do see a slasher movie that has any artistic merit whatsoever, it's easy to exaggerate its quality and see it as something more than what it is (i.e., House of Wax.) Seen in this perspective Valentine is actually one of the better examples of the genre I've seen, one of the few American slasher movies to approach the level of visual and stylistic sophistication found in the best Italian giallo. Director Jamie Banks is not yet on a par with Argento or Bava, but here he has crafted an atmospheric, entertaining thriller full of beautiful women, fiendish murders, and a truly inspired final gotcha. The script is full of tongue-in-cheek humor that kept me laughing out loud, but never sunk into the kind of self-referential, trendy hipster attitude that mars so many horror films made for Generation Y (i.e., Scream and its sequels). In the eighties most victims in horror flicks were anonymous starlets who never appeared in anything else, but since Drew Barrymore was butchered in Scream it has been increasingly common to cast familiar faces in the victim role. This film delivered spectacularly in that respect, with three truly beautiful women--Katherine Heigl, Jessica Caulfield, and Denise Richards (who received star billing!) meeting increasingly gruesome and inventive deaths. Ms. Richards' hot tub scene alone is worth the price of admission. It's become a cliché for the masked killer of beautiful women to turn out to be a chick herself, but Jessica Capshaw was believable as Dorothy. Marley Shelton, with her fetching girl next door wholesomeness (I loved her in sugar and spice) makes for an appealing last girl, and David Boreanaz was amusingly repellent as her alcoholic boy friend, at times resembling nothing so much as a junior varsity caricature of Jack Nicholson in The Shining. I give Valentine seven chainsaws--not as good as Blood and Black Lace but better than House of Wax. "},{"Title":"It Broke The Current Horror Movie Cliche","Date":"11 December 2003","Score":"2 out of 3 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  First off there are some spoilers in my comments.  Secondly, I am a huge horror movie fan.  I honestly feel only horror movie buffs can give good reviews as we know the material.  My opinion is honest, and not based on a dislike for the genre. Now on with my comments. Why did I love this movie?  First off, it's a holiday horror movie. I was reared on them in the late 80's with the VHS boom.  I especially love the Valentine theme.  Secondly, we are offered a cast of young adults as opposed to teens.  As a 20 something I can totally relate to the character's difficulties in the dating world. This helped define our characters.  It would have been easy to let the girls fall into the usual stereotypes of the pretty one, the smart one and sexy one etc.  By showcasing the difficulties of dating in an adult world, the cliched horror characters became people as opposed to cardboard cut outs.  Thirdly, you have to agree that the acting is great.  A good scary movie idea can be ruined by bad acting. Valentine is populated with a fresh, young, and attractive cast who can act.  This gives the movie an edge that many of its lower budget competitors could only pray at having.  For this and so much more I honestly love this movie.As for things I did not like?  Well there isn't much, but that annoying rhyming neighbor was as annoying as nails on a chalk board.  I think the movie could have done without him.  Even his murder was stupid.  Other then that I was pleased with the movie. Now what is the best aspect of this movie?  IT BROKE THE SCARY MOVIE CLICHE STARTED BY SCREAM!!!!  How many of you missed it?  Well here's the cliche.  From SCREAM (1996) on, so many horror movies ended with a killer telling the final girl or the would be survivors why they did the killings, and that they were going to frame so and so.  We saw this most notably in all the Scream movies, in both of the Urban Legend Films, and Do You Wanna Know A Secret.  Valentine seems to have confused people.  Many people left the theater thinking Dorothy was the killer, but she was not.  Adam was the killer.  He did what every killer in the fore mentioned movies set out to do.  He killed those who wronged them, and then he framed Dorothy for the murders.  This is evidenced by the blood dripping from Adams nose in the movie's closing scene. I love Valentine for so many reasons, and after you read my comments I am hoping you will like it just a little more.  Go on and vote for it. Give it your honest vote.  Mine was an 8. "},{"Title":"Banks' follow up to Urban Legend","Date":"18 February 2004","Score":"","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  Jamie Banks split critics with his debut movie; some called it brainlessly entertaining, whilst others just dismissed it as brainless. Looking back, Urban Legend was actually one of the better efforts that shamelessly jumped on the Scream bandwagon, good enough to garner a sequel and it showed that the director knew how to build tension and had an eye for neat photography.  For his follow up he put a popular and capable cast together, including Denise Richards and David Boreanaz, going back to the roots of the slasher genre's influences to terrorize an annual day of celebration. His choice - rather obviously - was St. Valentine's day, the same holiday that was (pick) axed in 1981 by director George Milhalka and his gas masked bogeyman - Harry Walden. Upon release My Bloody Valentine was rather ignored, but over the years it has gained a cult following for its foreboding location and the prospect that maybe one day fans will be able to see a full uncut copy that is supposed to be exquisitely packed with gore. Banks' Valentine isn't any kind of remake; in fact the only things that this has in common with its predecessor is the date for which the slaughter takes place and a few references. But I kind of hoped that they might both share the same endearing sense of fun too&#133;It starts with a pre-teen valentine disco set in 1988.  A bespectacled young boy heads on the dance floor looking for a young female to share a dance with. First he approaches Shelly (later played by Katherine Heigl) who embarrassingly rebuffs him. His charm doesn't seem to work with Lilly (Jessica Cauffer), Paige (Denise Richards) or Kate (Marley Shelton) either; they all send him packing quite arrogantly. His luck changes when Dorothy (Jessica Capshaw) actually acknowledges him and the twosome leave hand in hand. They are later caught kissing under a bench by a gang of bullies. In order to save her own self from persecution, Dorothy accuses the youngsters of attacking her and so the gang decides to take their own revenge. They cover him in red goo (Carrie?), strip him and chase him onto the dance floor where they proceed to beat him up. Hmmm, could that be the sort of thing to turn someone in to a violent mass murderer? Well of course&#133; Fast forward ten years and the girls are now women.  No one is sure what happened to Jeremy (the bullied brat from earlier) as he disappeared after that dance. It's close to Valentines Day and they each receive a card signed with a poetic threat to their lives. They soon realise to take them seriously when Shelly is found with her throat sliced. Before long a mysterious masked madman stalks each of them leaving Kate and her boyfriend Adam (David Boreanaz) to work out that she's next on the psycho's list&#133;     Firstly, this certainly looks the business. The healthy production values have been put to good use and the photography is excellent in places. The director also gains credit for the thought he puts into some of the shots. A dead girl falling over a banister and landing in an open bin, the scene in the art display was also smartly located, although perhaps he didn't make as good use of it as he could have. Most of the cast are exceptionally beautiful (Charlie Sheen's missus takes some beating) and they're better actors than most slasher alumni that usually plague similar themed efforts. But if ever the phrase &#145;looks aren't everything' could be applied specifically to a movie, and then this is that film. Basically, what we have here is pleasing eye candy without anything solid to back it up. Think of Jennifer Lopez and you'll know what I mean. Ok, take your mind off J-Lo now so we can get back to the film&#133; are you ready? Good. The murders are practically gore-less (perhaps an attempt to gain the most lenient rating possible?), which may have worked for Halloween because John Carpenter used precision to make sure that each killing was extremely suspenseful, but Jamie Banks hasn't bothered to include either. The first chase sequence was tight and brilliantly crafted, but the rest simply felt rushed and unplanned. The assassin does indeed look creepy in a cherub mask and the blood trickling from his nose after he dispatches each victim was a neat little touch. Nevertheless, there aren't enough of those pleasing elements to add up to a satisfying whole and mostly Valentine is as hollow as an Easter egg.Perhaps this could have worked as a mystery if you were lucky enough to see it at the cinema, although Warner Bros manage to ruin it for you on video by giving away the killer's identity on the back cover.   Another problem with Valentine is that the characters are all so self indulgent and morally extracted that it's almost impossibility for them to win over the audience. In the beginning they're shown as mockers to any child that's unfortunate enough to be less pretty than their egotistical selves and actually possess a brain. This discrimination continues throughout the movie as they brush off the men who are trying to woo them out on a date, simply because they're not up to their high standards. How can anyone want such pompously arrogant characters to survive? In a typical slasher movie, the &#145;final girl' is usually the shy reclusive type that the audience feels sympathetic towards, like Laurie Strode. These characters have no such power, leading you to believe that the world would be a better place without them anyway!Jamie Banks has proved that he has the potential to become a fair helmer, however I would consider this to be his first feature failure. It certainly didn't help that the cover description ruined the mystery for me, but even so, there's still little to recommend here. It's a shame that he couldn't have made more of the talented cast and competent budget, but in the end, Valentine just feels empty. A couple of talented cast members are not really enough to warrant the many obnoxious ones. Cupid certainly missed when he fired the arrow of fortune at this heart&#133;    "},{"Title":"Same old, same old...","Date":"10 February 2004","Score":"","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  ***Possible Spoiler*** This is MTV slasher nr 1000 something and it's just like the rest. "},{"Title":"Logic be damned, here comes Valentine!","Date":"18 May 2002","Score":"","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  There are so many puns to play on the title of the spectacularly bad Valentine that I don't know where to begin.  I will say this though; here is a movie that makes me long for the complexity of the Valentine cards we used to give out in elementary school.  You know, the ones with Batman exclaiming You're a super crime-fighting valentine!Valentine is a slasher movie without the slightest hint of irony, one of the few horror movies in recent years that ignores the influence of Scream.  The villain is omniscient and nigh-invulnerable.  The heroes are easily scared when people run around corners and grab them by the shoulders screaming HeyIjustleftmycoatbehind!  The score is more overbearing than Norman Bates' mother.The flimsy plot follows several childhood friends, now grown up and extremely curvaceous.  Since the film gives them nothing else to do, they stand around and wait until a masked stalker kills them one by one.  This stalker appears to be former nerd Jeremy Melton, who was constantly rejected by women and beaten by men in high school.  With Valentine's Day approaching, the women begin receiving scary cards foretelling their doom.  Melton seems like the obvious suspect.  Only problem is, as numerous characters warns, in thirteen years Melton could have changed his appearance to look buff and handsome.  So (insert terrified gasp here) everyone is a suspect!Here's problem one.  In order to have any sense of suspense while watching Valentine, you have to accept a reality in which a high school nerd is capable of becoming David Boreanaz.  Nerds don't turn into Angel when they grown up, they turn into older, balder nerds.  He's not a terrible actor, but the script, by no less than four writers, gives him and the rest of the cast nothing to do but scream and make out. Denise Richards (the bustiest  actress in Hollywood never to star in Baywatch) is especially exploited; most shamefully in the blatant excuse to get her in a bathing suit just before a crucial suspense scene.  Note to self  always bring a bathing suit to a Valentine's Day party.  Just because it's February doesn't mean you might not feel like taking a little dip.The slasher in Valentine dresses in head-to-toe black with a Cherub's mask.  Here's problem number two.  The filmmakers clearly thought this would be a disturbing image to have on the head of someone who's whacking people in the face with hot irons.  Plain and simple, it's not.  Instead, it just made me wonder how a guy with a mask that covers his entire face, including his eyes and ears, can move so stealthily without bumping his shins on chairs or tables.  Then again, given the things the Cupid Killer does, maybe he can teleport and his eyes are on his hands.  Not only is the movie bad, it isn't even sure who the killer is; the final twist is more Huh? than Hah!  When you're not scratching your head you're yawning, then groaning, then searching for the nearest exit.  Do not watch this movie.  Even if you're alone on Valentine's Day, find something, ANYTHING, else to do.  You'll be glad you did. "}{"Title":"Nothing new here","Date":"8 August 2001","Score":"","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  Its plain to see why the makers of Scary Movie found it so easy to spoof these 'teen slasher' movies. They are so unbelievably formulaic. And if Valentine had been released a year or so earlier, I'm sure they would have been spoofing this film too - that's if they found any actual original material to distinguish it from the Screams, I know what you did last summers, and Urban Legends.Valentine offers nothing new to this genre, except a better than usual ending which, of course, leaves lots of room for the inevitable sequel. As always, a masked psychotic killer stalks a bunch of beautiful young women, killing the main character's friends, one by one, in typically over the top style. Lots of T&A on display, no character development, bad acting, and overly elaborate bloodshed.The thing I can't stand about these kind of movies is that they pass themselves off as 'who done its?'. The thing is that they aren't because the motive is only revealed once the killer has unmasked, and tells the main character who's friends have now all been murdered. Usually something that was never made at all clear during the film anyway (eg. main character's mother's uncle's fishing partner kicked his friend's father's dog). Everybody still left alive throughout the film is a 'suspect', but they are more 'Red Herrings' than suspects. As we all know at this point the main character manages an implausible escape and kills the unmasked psycho killer after the motive is revealed.Valentine followed this formula almost to the letter. ***************SPOILER!!!!!! (mini spoiler anyway)*************** In Valentine the motive was not revealed, but more, left for you to think about given that the film didn't quite conclude in the typical 'teen slash' way. The issue is only part resolved, and the goal of the lead killer may or may not have been fulfilled by surviving the bloodshed and killing almost everybody. Will the killer want more, or were the demons truly vanquished?This still didn't make Valentine a good film, instead it simply saved it from being as bad as usual, which still doesn't count for much. To anybody thinking of making another film along these lines, please don't. Originality is so important, and its hard to see any originality coming out of this genre. "},{"Title":"What an awful mess.","Date":"30 July 2001","Score":"","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  here was no effort put into Valentine to prevent it from being just another teenage slasher film, a sub-genre of horror films of which we have seen entirely too many over the last decade or so. I've heard a lot of people complaining that the film rips off several previous horror movies, including everything from Halloween to Prom Night to Carrie, and as much as I hate to be redundant, the rip off is so blatant that it is impossible not to say anything. The punch bowl over poor Jeremy's head early in the film is so obviously taken from Carrie that they may as well have just said it right in the movie (`Hey everyone, this is the director, and the following is my Carrie-rip-off scene. Enjoy!'). But that's just a suggestion.(spoilers) The film is structured piece by piece exactly the same way that every other goofy teen thriller is structured. We get to know some girl briefly at the beginning, she gets killed, people wonder in the old oh-but-that-stuff-only-happens-to-other-people tone, and then THEY start to get killed. The problem here is that the director and the writers clearly and honestly want to keep the film mysterious and suspenseful, but they have no idea how to do it. Take Jason, for example. Here is this hopelessly arrogant guy who is so full of himself and bad with women that he divides the check on a date according to what each person had, and as one of the first characters seen in the film after the brief history lesson about how bad poor Jeremy was treated, he is assumed to carry some significance. Besides that, and more importantly, he has the same initials as the little boy that all the girls terrorized in sixth grade, and the same initials that are signed at the bottom of all of those vicious Valentine's Day cards. It is not uncommon for the audience to be deliberately and sometimes successfully misled by the behavior of one or more characters that appear to be prime suspects, and Jason is a perfect example of the effort, but not such a good example of a successful effort. Sure, I thought for a while that he might very well be the killer, but that's not the point. We know from early on that he is terrible with women, which links him to the little boy at the beginning of the film, but then in the middle of the film, he appears at a party, smiles flirtatiously at two of the main girls, and then gives them a hateful look and walks away, disappearing from the party and from the movie with no explanation. We already know he is a cardboard character, but his role in the film was so poorly thought out that they just took him out altogether when they were done with him.On the positive side, the killer's true identity was, in fact, made difficult to predict in at least one subtle way which was also, unfortunately, yet another rip-off. Early in the film, when Shelley stabs the killer in the leg with his own scalpel, he makes no sound, suggesting that the killer might be a female staying silent to prevent revealing herself as a female, rather than a male as everyone suspects. But then for the rest of the film, we just have this stolid, relentless, unstoppable killer with the emotionless mask and that gigantic butcher knife. Director Jamie Blanks (who, with all due respect, looks like he had some trouble with the girls himself in the sixth grade) mentions being influenced by Halloween. This is, of course, completely unnecessary, because it's so obvious from how badly he plagiarizes the film. The only difference between the killer in Valentine and Michael Meyer's is that Michael's mask was so much more effective and he didn't have a problem with nosebleeds. This stuff is shameless. At the end, there is a brief attempt to mislead us one more time as to who the killer is (complete with slow and drawn out `and-the-killer-is' mask removal), but then we see Adam's nose start to bleed as he holds Kate, his often reluctant girlfriend, and we know that he's been the killer all along. Nothing in the film hinted that he might be the killer until the final act, and these unexplained nosebleeds were not exactly the cleverest way to identify the true killer at the end of the film. Valentine is not scary (I watched it in an empty house by myself after midnight, and I have been afraid of the dark for as long as I can remember, and even I wasn't scared), and the characters might be possible to care about if it weren't so obvious that they were just going to die. I remember being impressed by the theatrical previews (although the film was in and out of the theater's faster than Battlefield Earth), but the end result is the same old thing. Over the years, I've had a love-hate relationship with teen-slasher films, especially those who came out after the incredible success of Scream. I like the Scream movies, and I found I Know What You Did Last Summer very entertaining, but apart from them (and Final Destination), the likes of The Faculty, Urban Legend and all those others, did not go too well with me. Frankly, I consider them inane rubbish. After having read promising reviews of Cherry Falls, I was deeply disappointed the abysmal feature itself, and considered there to be no hope the teen-slasher genre. Still, I went to see Valentine.Directed by Jamie Blanks of Urban Legend fame, there was very little about Valentine that gave the impression of an above-average thriller, and yet it is. What helps is that the material is taken seriously, there are no pop-culture references, in-jokes or post-modernism that has plagued most of recent teen-films. This film is a welcome return to the more genuine, old-fashioned films of the eighties, sometimes even reminiscent of Dario Argento, the master that Blanks is undoubtedly a fan of. Again, the film scores points for avoiding political-correctness; the victims are mostly women and, surprisingly, they're all white. The killer, wearing a cherub-mask that is at first silly, but becomes rather scary as the film goes on, never runs but ultimately catches his victims (in the grand tradition created by the original Mummy film) and proceeds in mutilating them in macabre ways, be it with a bow and arrow, electric screwdriver or a steam-iron, this killer is always interesting if only for the sake of knowing what instrument he'll use next!But what about the women he kills? The actresses in this movie are actresses whose names you will probably never know or never remember, but I was actually so impressed by a couple of them that I did learn their names... But then again, I didn't like them all. As hard as I try, I cannot seem to find anything good about Denise Richard's most recent performances. She was awful in The World is Not Enough and she's awful in this! While she was perfect for the sexy-sultry vixen of Wild Things, she's just not good at all in this movie. There are moments when she's adequate, but most of the time the dialogue that comes from her mouth seems forced, unreal and pretentious. The other actresses fare much better. Marley Shelton makes a fine protagonist while the two Jessicas, Capshaw and Cauffiel, are easily the stars of the group. Both are very natural and give good performances. Katherine Heigl is in the movie for such a short time that it's really not worth mentioning her, but she was also good in her part. The real problem, performance-wise, comes from the terrible miscasting of David Boreanaz. He's just painful to watch sometimes, too stiff and too wooden - and he's playing a character that's supposed to be much younger than he is!Jamie Blanks directs the film with some style, though never going over-the-top in his visuals. The film has a cool, toned-down look and feel to it and is cold and steely. I really liked the visual aspect of the film. The killer wears a cherub mask and he uses a bow in one scene, another scene has one of the victims' puddle of blood looking remarkably like a heart, and the list goes on. Still, despite what sound like a rave review from me, I found a number of flaws with the film. The killer's original appearance is so sudden, and the sight of the mask may cause some audiences to laugh. Many of the victims are secondary characters that add nothing at all to the plot other than a number to add to the body-count. As a result, we don't really care about many of the characters that are killed, and the suspense Blanks tries to conjure fails.However, if it weren't for one thing then all of the things above would be meaningless and not worthy talking about. This thing is suspense, and Valentine has loads of it. I was so surprised to feel the suspense in this film as I had not felt something like it for a while, and certainly not in a film of this genre. So, all in all, it must be said that this movie works! Forget the stupid plotting, forget the crappy dialogue, turn off your brain and go with the show and you might find yourself enjoying it immensely. I did, and I'm not going to apologize for it.7.5/10  "},{"Title":"I loved this film, esp. "},{"Title":"Well, the soundtrack was interesting...","Date":"10 February 2001","Score":"","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" Something has gone horribly wrong when you find yourself paying attention to the songs featured on a horror film's soundtrack. Case in point Valentine. I was quite thrilled to hear the delightfully morbid (although somewhat obvious) Valentine's Day by Marilyn Manson during an otherwise excruciatingly boring party scene.There was something interesting going on in the film's look, stylistically slick and in gratuitous homage to Dario Argento. Unfortunately, Valentine is cursed with your basic interchangeable revenge plot. Kid is spurned, kid grows up, kills the lovely ones who spurned him. Or (yawn) is it (yawn) really (yawwwn) him??? After a perfunctory Scream-esquire introduction where a female med student on a seemingly deserted college campus is butchered...in the morgue, no less...the attention shifts to four emotionally void bitches (except for one who's kinda sweet inside) who are low on character and high on sex appeal (if you happen to be a praying mantis, that is).The girls are stalked and murdered between what seems like oceans of yawn-inducing dialogue, until we have the obligatory Scream-esquire party scene where all of our characters are gathered together so that we may cut to the chase, so to speak. Doesn't anyone just rent a remote cabin at Camp Crystal Lake for this kind of thing?Gratuitous lapses in logic abound, and below you will find my favorites- the first victim in the film is preparing for an autopsy on a corpse. She's lured out of the operating theater by a strange noise, and when she returns, the killer has cleverly disguised himself as the naked, sheet-covered corpse on which she was going to work. The killer (SURPRISE!) leaps at her from the table, at which point she turns around to cower, and he vanishes...only to reappear seconds later fully clothed and wearing a mask. Uh...OK. Are all of these people quick-change artists?- one particularly boring sequence takes place in an apparently cavernous apartment, where an apparently unfathomably rich artist has constructed an unbelievably boring maze of video monitors. Although the party is teeming with guests, nobody happens to be in the maze when our beloved killer appears to dispatch another victim. Not only does he seem to know the exact layout of the maze and how to change it to trap his quarry, but he fires several arrows into her body, causing her to stagger backwards through a hidden emergency exit and into a stairwell, where she tumbles over the balcony and falls about seven stories down the stairwell into a waiting dumpster, which closes on impact. It's an admittedly bravura murder, but incredibly dumb, too (I didn't even mention the fact that he managed to walk into a crowded party wearing a mask and carrying a bow and arrow, unnoticed). Oh and by the way...the victim is not even missed, because she was (get this) on her way from the party to the airport to go on a business trip! HAR!!!- near the climax of the film, the detective in charge of the case races to the big Valentine's Day party, convinced the killer is there and can be apprehended. Unfortunately, he doesn't bother to call for backup, and...whoops! His beheaded corpse means help is nowhere in sight for our imperiled heroine. Oh brother. And while I'm at it...since when can you actually hear someone's voice mail picking up a call just by holding their cell phone?I could go on, but...I think the point has been made. The movie is very obviously padded, inserting obvious red herrings such as a confusing scene where Paige allows herself to be lured into an upstairs bedroom with the promise of sex, and when sex is offered she reacts with stunned revulsion, taking up five minutes of screen time to enact her revenge on the poor guy. There is a totally unnecessary character who shows up to be tossed through an Argento-esque glass shower door, one of the film's most inspired moments. The violence in this movie is intense; there are some horrific throat-gougings and even a face being burned with a hot iron. None of it looks or seems the least bit real, and strangely, none of it has much impact. This movie made me feel like an unshockable veteran of a bloody war.But no matter. "},{"Title":"Never leave power tools next to hot tubs","Date":"30 June 2015","Score":"","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" It's fair to say that 1997's 'Scream' reinvented the 'slasher' genre, breathing new life into something that was pretty formulaic and predictable. Then, four years later we have 'Valentine,' &#x96; a slasher movie that feels as if it belongs somewhere in the eighties at best. Either that or no one on the entire production staff ever watched Scream or knew about its existence.The beauty of Scream was that it listed all the clichés associated with the horror genre and did its best to subvert them. Valentine, on the other hand, seems to want to adhere to every cliché and be totally predictable.At the start of the movie we see a flashback from yesteryear where a geeky looking boy was (slightly!) bullied at a school prom by a gang of girls and then beaten up by some boys. Skip forward twenty or so years and he's out for revenge on the girls he perceived as his tormentors. Here's the first thing I noticed... I know we're hardly meant to feel empathy towards the (as yet unknown) killer, but these girls didn't really do enough to warrant their grisly executions. Perhaps that's meant to make us hate him more, I don't know. I'd have thought he'd need more of a reason towards his hated. I know there are some brief explanations regarding how he was sent away to an institution after the 'attack' but it's all pretty glossed over.So, the film is basically the adult girls being stalked and eliminated one by one. Naturally, they all hang out with a multitude of unsavoury men, designed to make us wonder which one is really the killer in 'disguise.' Another thing you may notice is the heavy marketing towards Denise Richards. I know nowadays it's a bit fashionable to hate her, but, back at the end of the nineties, she was pretty hot (commercial) property. Unfortunately, she's not really the star. This is a shame because she's actually quite fun and is by far the most memorable character on screen.The death scenes (bar one regarding the hot tub) are nothing special and certainly not imaginative and you'll probably guess who the killer is simply because you will. It's just obvious somehow, despite attempts at misdirection.You're really going to have to enjoy slasher films to really like this. Either that or just want to see Denise Richards in her prime! Otherwise, stick to Scream, its sequels and any vaguely better slasher flick. "},{"Title":"One Bloody Little Valentine's Massacre.","Date":"14 February 2007","Score":"1 out of 2 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" An obscure but overall nice effort in the genre, Valentine is a great movie for people who don't like Valentine's Day. The film opens with a scene from a junior high school Valentine's dance, where a nerdy young boy is rejected a dance from some prettier, more popular girls, and is ultimately humiliated and beaten-up in front of his fellow classmates. Now, years later, the same group of girls who attended their school years together are being stalked by a knife-wielding maniac, whose first victim is a medical student that was also friends with the girls. The psychopath behind the murders, hidden behind a cherub mask, begins following each of the women, and more and more of them begin to disappear. It's up to the remaining women to discover the killer's identity before they become another one of his victims... could the killer be, perhaps, the boy whose life they made a living hell years earlier? Not quite as good as the 1981 slasher romp My Bloody Valentine, but also much different, Valentine is a surprisingly original little horror movie. The entire stalker thing has been done before, but it is uniquely presented here and is really interesting. Jamie Blanks, the director of Urban Legend, also directs this film, and is both stylish and consistent. The entire movie uses a lot shades of red, not only hinting at the entire Valentine's Day theme, but also going along with the color of blood. There are some very inventive sequences (among them being the entire love maze that the Lily character takes her friends to), and the deaths are really creative, providing an interesting way to kill off the characters. There are some clichés to be found in this slasher flick though, and they will be easily spotted - not nearly as many clichés as I was expecting though.The film's creepy villain (dressed in a jet-black trench coat and masked with a cherub face that is actually very scary looking) uses a wide array of weapons - knives, axes, drills - and of course, a bow and arrow! All of these scenes are very well executed, and obviously the writers wanted to think up some really creative ways to kill people - the hot tub scene was one of them! The acting in the film was decent. The cast consists of numerous beautiful (but ill-fated) young women, and I didn't have a problem with the performances. They could have been better in some aspects, but overall the acting was good. I was guessing the killer's identity throughout the film, and the shocking but abrupt conclusion was a wonderful way to end the film. It was unexpected and kind of leaves you hanging there, but I liked that.Overall, Valentine is an above-average slasher film. I'm a little surprised at the low user rating, I'd assumed this would have ranked at least a 5.0 average. Don't let the bad user reviews put you off though, this is a slasher movie worth looking at for horror fans. It has some very nice creativity thrown into it and a good plot line to boot. Sure, it's a bit clichéd, but it tries to be original and is a good step in the right direction. It's not perfect, but watch it for yourself, and then judge it. If anything, it's a fun little holiday-oriented splatter movie. 7/10. "}{"Title":"Because the skinny little geek with the glasses is always the greatest threat","Date":"17 August 2003","Score":"1 out of 2 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  Final Score 0.7 (out of 10)'Valentine' not only manages to be a bottom-of-the-barrel slasher movie full of missed opportunities, but takes that extra step over the ledge in being stereotypical, conformist and completely predictable to the point of being offensive.I'm going to break my rule (once again) and describe the plot a bit just to show how fundamentally wrong-headed and ridiculous this all is. It opens at a high school Valentine's Day dance where we meet a kid (whose appearance is jammed with so many `nerd clichés' he is hard to take as anything halfway resembling a real person) asking all the pretty girls to dance. As he ends up making out with `the fat chick', the two are caught by punks. `The fat girl' accuses `the nerd' of attacking her so that when the punks strip him down to his underwear and beat the snot out of him it is to be seen as somewhat noble.  The kids at the dance stand around them yelling Fight despite that it is clearly a gang beating.  Fast forward (a number of years I cannot remember) as our nerd has replaced his glasses with a creepy Cupid mask with a bulked out Michael Myers-type of body. Apparently with no life or just completely psychotic he now goes on a killing spree against the girls that rejected him - not the punks who beat him up, mind you, because the movie wants to say that the relationship is the be-all and the loss of a relationship is more traumatizing then even a gang beating. Still with me? The movie shows us this first scene of cruelty and then flips it 180 degrees having the A-group be the victims and expects us to go along with it. It is a nonsensical dichotomy that Hollywood loves to pander to this crowd and at the same time masochistically brutalizes them.I will give the movie one tiny prop. It busts a little cliché in it's first death involving the age-old bit where a character (Bride of Chucky's Katherine Heigl) hides among a room of cadavers. I was kind of glad to see the bit (which I will not spoil) promptly squashed in a  realistic and rather sickening way. However, it set me up for a more brutal, more daring horror movie that this one turns out to be.  Much of the pre-death moments involve the characters wandering around looking for the source of noises set to dull monotonous musical clanks. They wander on and on, long past the point it would have been suspenseful. Those pretty girls grow up to be Marley Shelton ('Sugar & Spice' hottie), Jessica Capshaw, Jessica Cauffiel and Denise Richards. Usually counted on to a movie's babe factor in the likes of Starship Troopers and Wild Things, here Richards look to be infected with parasites that have made her frail and malnourished. Capshaw as `the fat girl grown up' grapples with her guilt over framing the nerd. The story focus primarily on her until the final few minutes when it awkwardly derails and hack screenwriter Donna Powers decides she wants this to be Shelton's movie. It doesn't matter anyway because everybody keeps their clothes on the entire time, the movie cuts away from sex scenes as though it was an NBC sitcom - unaware that that guilty pleasure aspect would have ratcheted the movie up to being watchable on at least one level.`Valentine' was directed by Jamie Blanks who previously helmed `Urban Legend', a diverting slasher movie in the wake of the `Scream' craze that I truly enjoyed to my own surprise. 'Legend' was playful and  inventive with it's gore and Blanks gave the movie a stylish look. A startling contrast to this movie which tries to make up for it's uninspired nature with the fierce brutality of the violence (and the killer). It gives us an unrelentingly repressive atmosphere, dull and dreary, right up until the final scene - a supposed twist that is telegraphed far in advance (the killer can only be 1 of 1 people). The movie is hollow and drags, but I will let the final score speak for itself on this aspect.A more talented writing team might have noticed and explored that a horror movie set against a love story/Valentine's Day backdrop could have made for an inventive mix and some delicious moments of irony. Instead, `Valentine' wants to play it straight, forcing itself into the same old template Hollywood's obsession with the high school A-group, and it's attitude that life stops and starts (literally, in this case) with the success or failure of people's relationships. Blanks has done herself a retroactive favor the more movies like this come out and immediately go to the bottom of the genera pile - the more I feel reinforced that  `Urban Legend` really was good as I thought. Easily, one of the worst movies of the new decade. Wes Craven style nudge nudge wink wink ironic smirking gets stale pretty fast, so if someone decides to STILL make a slasher movie all these years later, after all the rip offs and inferior variations on a (very limited) theme, you would think they would have some kind of fresh spin on the genre, or at the very least a decent script, memorable dialogue, and interesting characters. And then along came the various sequels as well as several copycats, as was the case back then.  Valentine is the latest.       Hey, remember that kid that everyone was mean to and ignored back in school?  Yeah, we all know the type.  Anyway, in this film, we are introduced to a group of young, buxom women who also knew the type.  They consist of Paige (Denise Richards), Kate (Marley Shelton), Dorothy (Jessica Capshaw), and Lily (Jessica Cauffiel).  They all seem to lead very happy lives, enjoying their sexual, predatory vixen skills to the fullest.  But when their mutual friend, Shelley (Katherine Heigl), is brutally murdered, the girls all begin to receive menacing valentines from a mysterious killer who walks around in a Cupid mask.         Now, as the girls begin to get picked off one by one, they,along with Kate's on-again-off-again beau, Adam (David Boreanaz), must unmask the murderer before it's too late.       Based on Tom Savage's non-slasher novel of the same title, Valentine is definitely a true slasher at heart.  The film has good intentions, and the premise is quite original, but it just makes one mistake after another.       Starting with the all too obvious kill-a-celebrity-right-in-the-beginning scenario, Valentine has trouble gaining any redeeming qualities.  The sequence of events is so shamefully predictable that it's hard to imagine what poor Mr. Savage must be thinking (Who would do such an awful thing to my book?!).       The characters in the film are so flat and detestable that we really just wish every single one of them would die so that we could leave the theater already.The acting is standard horror fare.  Denise Richards once again shows us her amazing and wide-range acting talents  Those two large things attached to the front side of her body that we like to call breasts.  David Boreanaz gives a fair performance, but definitely shouldn't give up his day job on the WB's Angel.  Newcomer Marley Shelton can't do much with her underwritten role, and she comes off as extremely annoying and whiny for the most part.  The rest of the acting is close to pitiful.       Jamie Blanks's direction is unquestionably a few steps down from 1998's superior horror film, Urban Legend.       Valentine is most certainly a pretty bad film.  Though fun and actually, sort of, kind of, somewhat scary, it never goes where it might have been able to go with its clever premise. So I give the film credit for trying.  But like most other films that have tried to follow in Screams footsteps, it does fail quite miserably.Valentine is a story about a geeky kid that just wants to be accepted in the sixth grade.  He is at a dance and asks all the pretty girls to dance and they all say no.  Some of them are disgustingly mean to him and tell him that they would rather be boiled alive than to dance with him ( guess how that character dies? ).  Then one heavy set girl decides she will make out with him and then when all the popular guys catch her doing it, she says that he forced himself on her and they beat the tar out of him and he is sent to reform school.  That is the beginning and it is well done.  It sets up the killer on the loose with a revenge plot quite nicely.  We of course skip ahead about 15 years and we have beautiful women in college lined up to be slaughtered.  The opening death is extremely laughable but has its moments of nice touches and subtle homages to films like Halloween.  It is worth mentioning how the first woman is killed because it is a lesson in horror mythology of all the wrong things to do to attract a killer on the loose on a college campus.A young woman just comes back from a disasterous date and decides that she is going to go do an autopsy at 11 o clock at night.  Then to top it off, she is wearing a flimsy tank top, has large breasts and she decides to keep the lights off in the autopsy room, because, well you know, you don't need light to disect a human being.  I started to ask myself why she was allowed to disect a corpse with no supervision this late and with no lights on seeing as she was only a med student.  Horror movies are always filled with silly situations ( Friday the 13th's, no one wipes after they are finished in the bathroom, people always go to investigate noises and so on ) but this is one of the sillier ones.  Then when she is grabbed by the corpse, instead of leaving, she stays in the room to see who it is.  And then when the things chases her, she doesn't go for the door, she tries to hide in the other rooms.  DUMB! DUMB! Nothing really jumps out at you.   I think Jamie Blanks has an idea of what it takes to scare an audience, he has probably tried to emulate many of the greats like Raimi, Hitchcock and Carpenter, but he can't quite seem to hit the perfect note.  Maybe if he keeps trying he will get it because there are scenes in here that are close to perfection but then they end too abruptly or without the proper pay off.  That is what made Halloween so elusive in it's brilliance.  The pay off was so horrific and so perfect that to try to duplicate it is almost unfathomable.  Valentine comes close but ultimately fails.This is not as bad as some horror out there but it is not in the same league as some of the new horror films that have made audiences embrace horror again. "},{"Title":"There's worse ones out there","Date":"23 May 2007","Score":"0 out of 1 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" Valentine is a really underrated and actually decent slasher film.**SPOILERS**Friends since High School, Paige Prescott, (Denise Richards) Kate Davies, (Marley Shelton) Dorothy Wheeler, (Jessica Capshaw) and Lily Voight, (Jessica Cauffiel) are shocked to learn the murder of a friend of theirs. Meeting up with Kate's boyfriend Adam Carr, (David Boreanaz) at the funeral, they are told from Det. Leon Vaughn, (Fulvio Cecere) if they'd help him with evidence in the case. As they get tormented by a series of strange valentine cards, old friend Campbell Morris, (Daniel Cosgrove) arrives in their lives as more strange deaths follow. Thinking back to their time together in an attempt to figure out who could've been behind the killings, they each have conflicting choices as to their identity, and when the killer targets them at a special gala party being held, they have to work to stay away from the killer and solve their identity.The Good News This was a nicely surprising and enjoyable film. One of the most surprising is that the film has some really great stalking scenes. There's really no better example than the opening kill, where a victim is dispatched inside a morgue. This is just insanely creepy, as the darkness and ever-present fear of death is executed perfectly, making it seem that every second spent was used to watch, and then the realization that there is someone there amps up the dread even more, and the chase around is simply nerve-rattling. Another one inside a maze of very weird videos along the walls, filled with closeups on faces, lips and eyes is another standout for being originally bizarre and suspenseful at the same time. The final chase through the house does have some tense moments as well, and the set-up for the jacuzzi doesn't really disappoint either. Other non-stalking suspense scenes show up throughout as well. The death scenes weren't all that novel, but are thankfully shockingly brutal, especially the attack where one of the victims in a wet bikini is trapped inside a jacuzzi with the killer jabbing at them through the cover with a power-drill. There's also a brutal slit throat, a decapitation and an ax in the shoulder blade as well, even though they're really that bloody or gory. It's simply the brutality that gets them noticed. There are a few other fairly decent ideas in the film too. The most inspiring is the idea of the killer sending his victims valentines cards with a twist. While not in the least bit an original idea, it's just refreshing to see some brutality brought back in the genre There was a cool killer disguise and that mask looked somewhat too freaky too. There's been far worse slashers along the way than this one.The Bad News There isn't a whole lot wrong here. The biggest is that film doesn't play the valentine-cards angle up very well and only half-heartedly develops the valentine-related novelty deaths angle. The card idea wasn't developed as much as it could have been, as if the film was waiting for a human-heart-in-a-box moment which never materialized ad was disappointing given the essence of the story. It felt like it could've gone much further than it went here, and after being introduced in the beginning, disappears from the second half and is never really introduced or mentioned again. Its greater failing is when it comes to the premise of a humiliated nerd who is getting revenge on the women who belittled him at the school dance. This is solid enough slasher movie motivation but then when it suits the film, it has the killer not just targeting the people he is after but anybody else &#150; boyfriends, witnesses, even someone found inside one girls' apartment. There's a sense of randomness in here that doesn't seem to be there from the others that have been influenced from before. The other last big problem is that the decidedly toned down nature, specifically it's gore and sleaze, should've been in abundance but seem mainly dried up here. The brutality of the deaths meant that there should've been a lot more graphic, and the sexiness of the women and the situations present shouldn't have been so tame. This will be the one that harms it the most amongst the real fans.The Final Verdict As there's really a decided lack of the real attracting elements in this film, it's got a real underrated feel even though there's some good elements here. Give it a shot if you've got an open mind or want to see a really harmless film, but hardcore horror fans of the past might not like this one all that much.Rated R Graphic Violence, Graphic Language and Brief Nudity "},{"Title":"Cupid's arrow misses the mark","Date":"21 December 2006","Score":"0 out of 1 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" When Halloween started off the trend of stalker/slasher movies, it proved to be something of a mixed blessing. For every inventive classic like Halloween and A Nightmare On Elm Street, you get an equally bad knockoff like Friday the 13th. Scream, another classic kick-started the whole genre off again with a distinctly postmodern spin. And now we have Valentine, a horror film that falls somewhere in between competent and dire.As the title suggests, the theme in question is Valentines Day. But don't get your hopes up. Valentine will never do for February 14th what Halloween did for October 31st. Everything about the film is derivative. Which might have been just about bearable if it tried some of the postmodern referential irony Scream did so well. But it doesn't.In a prologue that 'borrows' from Carrie, Jeremy Melton, a social outcast is humiliated at a high school dance when all the girls scorn him. When he is caught in an embarrassing clinch with Dorothy, a fat girl, she turns on him saying he forced himself on her. The rest of the kids grab him, and beat the holy crap out of him.That sets the scene for the horrors to come. 13 years later the girls who turned Jeremy down have all grown into beautiful (not to mention shallow) women. And on Valentines Day, Jeremy's decided to look them up. Cue novelty death sequences, innocent girls walking down dark corridors and lots and lots of blood and gore.Aside from the Valentines Day gimmick, there is nothing remotely original about Valentine. A killer wearing a Cupid mask (Halloween), a long list of red herrings and possible suspects (Scream), it just goes on and on.Director Jaime Blanks is certainly a stylish director. And to his credit, he keeps events going at a snappy pace. But Valentine is nothing special. It doesn't revolutionise Valentine's Day the way Halloween did for its holiday.In regards to the cast, they're merely adequate. Marley Shelton is OK as the virtuous Kate, but there's nothing about her performance that really stands out. Although she can look genuinely terrified. Jessica Capshaw is undistinguished, and the way the film sets up her character for a surprise shock ending merely comes out as bizarre. And as for David Boreanaz, what a performance! Or lack, thereof.He's pretty much anonymous. He's a very bland screen presence. His performance is practically phoned in. Bizarre, considering he's the villain of the piece. Which is all the more shocking after seeing his work elsewhere. Boreanaz was probably trying to branch out in other areas while he was doing his TV work. And when he's played the villain in Buffy the Vampire Slayer and Angel, it's something he does very well. In Valentine. Not so much. He may have a limited range as an actor, but he usually plays the role of the villain with relish. Its odd then that he's so underwhelming here.The one bright spot in Valentine is Denise Richards. Out of all the cast, she's the most fun to watch. She gives the film much needed energy and lights up the screen whenever she's around as the nymphomaniac Paige. When she dies, the film dies along with her I'm afraid.Valentine has a few novelty touches, and there are some welcome bursts of humour that crop up from time to time (courtesy of Richards), but its a fairly forgettable venture. Moderately diverting the first time around, but nothing to capture your heart. "},{"Title":"Last gasp of the multiplex 'slasher' cycle?","Date":"18 January 2005","Score":"0 out of 1 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" VALENTINE Aspect ratio 2.391Sound formats Dolby Digital / DTS / SDDSRoses are red / Violets are blue / They'll need dental records / To identify you... (USA/Australia - 2001) Several years after an incident at the high school prom sent a teenage boy into a spiral of depression and insanity, the perpetrators - a number of bitchy, upwardly-mobile young women - receive strange Valentine cards from an unknown 'admirer' who promptly murders them, one by one.Signalling the last gasp of the late-90's/early-00's 'slasher revival', VALENTINE was a sophomore outing for director Jamie Blanks, whose URBAN LEGEND (1998) at least scored points for its visual flair. Here, Blanks is saddled with a derivative script and a cast of unlikable characters, whose monstrous vanity makes it impossible for viewers to care about their eventual fates (even the detective charged with finding the killer turns out to be a lecherous sleazeball!). Adapted from a novel by Tom Savage - whose complex narrative was reduced to its most basic components during the transfer from page to screen - the movie substitutes endless dialogue exchanges for plot and character development, and with the exception of an unpleasant sequence in which über-babe Denise Richards is attacked in a jacuzzi, the murder set-pieces are routine by slasher standards. This may have been due to Warner Bros.' insistence on the removal of extraneous violence, which makes no sense in the context of an R-rated horror movie (perhaps they were hoping for a PG-13?). Performances are uniformly fine, especially Jessica Capshaw (daughter of Kate Capshaw) as the former 'fat girl' who still resents the bullying she endured in high school, despite slimming her way into the affections of the very people who made her life a misery in the first place. Towards its half-baked finale, the film's multi-authored (!) screenplay points the finger of suspicion at all remaining cast members, including David Boreanaz (TV's Angel), playing an abusive alcoholic whose ex-girlfriend is on the killer's hit-list, though the climactic rampage is too reliant on illogical contrivances to be entirely effective. "},{"Title":"Decent slasher, some good scares","Date":"30 October 2004","Score":"0 out of 1 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" The slasher genre were the new craze in the late 70's and throughout the 80's. In the early 90's, it pretty much died down. Then Scream came, in 1996, and rejuvenated the genre with a film that was half-slasher, half a parody of slashers. Over the last few years, there have been quite a few slashers, most of them mediocre. When I found out that this was done by Jamie Blanks, the director of one of my favorite of the new slashers, Urban Legend, I immediately wanted to see it. It wasn't that disappointing, but it wasn't really great either. The plot is decent, but the pacing isn't very good. On repeated viewings, many of the early scenes(and plenty of the later ones as well) are kind of dull and boring. The acting is decent, but several of the big names are kind of disappointing, compared to earlier roles. The characters are pretty much just the typical clichés and stereotypes of the genre. The script is somewhat poor, and doesn't manage to keep your interest on more than one viewing(if even that). The film does have some good scares, some decent suspense and a little tension. The twist is far too obvious, though. On my first viewing, I saw it with a friend, and about half-way into the film, he had figured out who the killer was. The film has some pretty good death scenes, some of the best of the newer slashers, in my opinion(much like Blanks' other film, Urban Legend), but they are also the only really great thing about the film, and they are not really worth paying to see the film for. All in all, a decent slasher, but not one that is particularly worth watching. I recommend it only to big fans of the genre, Jamie Blanks or the actors. Anyone else should probably skip it, unless you really enjoy watching slasher flicks for the sole purpose of seeing well-done death scenes(which is fine, of course... I watched it for that very reason). If that's what you want from this film, you won't be disappointed. "},{"Title":"A stab in the right direction","Date":"25 July 2004","Score":"0 out of 1 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  Valentine to some of the major league critics was seen as another forgettable addition to the horror genre with little originality or substance back upon its release in 2001.In some ways I would have to agree with these general comments made, as I can't believe that Warner Brothers decided to make the film with its unoriginal and unintelligent storyline when there are so many genuinely great and intelligent horror films made that don't even make it to the cinema. The result is a very average formula horror film that does however posses some tense and sometimes even slightly scary moments that are all part of a storyline that although has little substance does at least prove to be of a better and more enjoyable standard than many others. This therefore serves one of a film's main purposes which is to just be an enjoyable experience for its audience.What also ensures that the audience won't immediately forget the film after watching it is the ending where the audience IS still left guessing as to who the killer is in a genuinely macabre ending. "},{"Title":"Half clone, half original - with a bit of homage thrown in","Date":"22 October 2001","Score":"0 out of 1 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  Reading most of the user comments of this film, I can't help but notice that many say it is a rip-off and complain that there is a lack of originality and character development. Even more groan-inducing were some peoples' superficial comments regarding Katherine Heigl's weight or the number of females in the film. Are those really valid reasons to dismiss a movie?Firstly what do you expect? Directors and studios cannot be blamed for adhering to well-established formulae when people like you (and me, for that matter) go and see them in droves. Instead of dismissing the film as a mere clone *after* you have seen it, perhaps you should expect nothing and be pleasantly surprised when a spark of originality does come up.Because this film in particular has more of it than most. OK - so there is a killer in a mask who stalks and kills in a variety of ways. But seriously there has to be a number of deaths in a horror film, and how else is it going to be achieved? OK, so perhaps the mask is a cliché that could have been abandoned. Or certainly improved - that supposed cherub face did nothing for me.As far as characterisation goes, there is a fair amount considering the ninety minute length. The character of Dorothy, although slightly stereotyped, is somewhat intriguing and portrayed admirably by Jessica Capshaw. Denise Richards, despite the claims of many, did the best with what she was given.One of the most original aspects of this film is the lack of a singularly defined protagonist. There is no Sidney Prescott/Laurie Strode heroine who is targeted but virtually invincible. The screen time is devoted equally to a few of the characters. One effect of this is that you never quite know who will be next or what certain character's motives are. This adds to the overall strength of the denouement - which is one of the best endings that I have seen for a long time in a film of this genre .The fact that Valentine contains references to Carrie, as well as many slasher films from the eighties, is neither annoying nor outstanding. Such touches can be effective, and as long as it is a step away from the ironic, in-jokey, post-modern Scream-type slasher (which was fine while it lasted, but has become overdone), then there is nothing wrong with it.Overall, a very entertaining and stylish movie. It is much better than Blanks' Urban Legend, which was itself a fine film in some places. The only thing that could spoil this film now is a sequel. And I love sequels. "},{"Title":"Your usual teen slasher movie, but does offer some good material. ** (out of four)","Date":"12 February 2001","Score":"0 out of 1 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  VALENTINE / (2001) ** (out of four)By this time in American cinema many audience members will expect Valentine, the most recent in the genre of teen slasher flicks, to be a recycled and half-witted horror movie. It most certainly fits that description, but I am coming to a point in which I am starting to feel sympathy for individuals who make this kind of movie. Nearly every teen slasher film is a rehearse of the one preceding it, so should I continue to hold the recycling of material against the filmmakers?Valentine is all that you would expect in a movie with the tag line of love hurts. The movie contains the standard slasher gimmick; this one takes place near Valentine's Day and uses the holiday spirit as a means to make people suffer. It contains the good-looking female cast of young women in their twenties, including Denise Richards, Jessica Capshaw, Jessica Cauffiel, and Marley Shelton. They play the moronic victims of love letters featuring threatening poems and disgusting pranks from a mystery admirer, so to speak. The production also inhabits the standard character stupidity, involving such reused scenes as a potential victim hearing noises outside her hotel, and investigating with only a towel around her waist. Lets not forget the scenes where the characters travel down long, dark hallways without even bothering to turn on the lights. Nobody is developed and there are no memorable lines or sequences, only the typical jump scenes and violent encounters that leave unsuspecting individuals dead with puddles of blood surrounding their corpses.This motion picture also borrows a few ideas from the original Carrie as well. The concept of an innocent boy mocked and wrongfully accused by the girls when they were in the sixth grade is a major plot point in the movie. That alleged culprit is not the only potential suspect in the lineup. There is also a strange detective (Fulvio Cecere) investigating the case, and one of the girl's alcoholic boyfriend (David Boreanaz), or maybe a weirdo audiovisual artist (Johnny Whitworth), or the greedy Internet entrepreneur (Daniel Cosgrove), currently living with one of the girls.We know from the opening scene that there will be a person in a mask picking his victims off one by one, using various methods of murder; knifes, a power-drill, an ax, a bow and arrow, glass shards, and more weapons of choice. We can easily identify the next victim, which is one of the only things that keep us interested in the movie, because there is no where near enough story to fill the hour and a half of situations. Nor is there a large enough selection of suspects to choose from, so we can have fun guessing the identity of the killer. The potential psychopaths are not adequately developed, so even out of the few characters provided I didn't even bother to guess. Even after the movie I was unsure of the killer's identity.There are a few things about Valentine that I actually did like. The slasher sequences are well executed, not as gruesome as you might expect, and all of the violence is in context. The killer abides by motive and circumstance; there are no meaningless slays. The plot is consistent in that area, and for once the killer's motives are clear to use, not just stuck in the ending to fill our inquiring curiosity. There are moments of suspense and surprise, and I liked the cast; the performers fill their characters with interest and zest.Jamie Blanks directed Valentine, and it is not a shock that his only other film is Urban Legend, another teen slasher movie. I take a guilty pleasure in movies of this gender; the Friday the 13th series includes some of my favorites and I am ashamed of liking the critically mauled I Know What You Did Last Summer.I guess there is an audience who will undoubtedly enjoy Valentine, and for better or worse, it doesn't take itself too seriously. I just have a hard time recommending a movie that follows so close to its proceeding counterparts in Friday the 13th the killer wore a hockey mask; in Scream the killer wore a ghost mask; in I know What You Did Last Summer, the killer wore a rain coat; in Urban Legends Final Cut, the killer wore a fencing mask; and in Valentine the killer wares what other than the mask of a cupid. See the similarities? What's next, a movie called Easter Horrors with a killer dressed as a big bunny delivering threatening decorated eggs? Or The Holiday Scream with a killer looking like Santa Claus giving horrific gifts? I might have just given some producers a few ideas. God Forgive me. "},{"Title":"Roses are red, violets are blue, the cast look embarrassed, and you would be, too","Date":"17 November 2001","Score":"1 out of 3 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":"  This is a stupid film, written and shot on autopilot.  It has the same faults as every other thoughtlessly produced slasher flick.  For the most part, people know what these are, but one of them seems to have gone unremarked the constant use of electronic mood noises.  You know the kind of thing.  It's a suspense scene, with the heroine walking around in the dark.  What do we hear?  Well, for the most part, we don't hear the ambient noises the heroine hears or imagines herself to hear (footsteps, creaking doors, rain outside, whatever).  We don't hear the musical score.  We don't even hear nothing.  What we hear is a high-pitched synthesised cricket-chirp - or low-pitched synthesised booms, or some such.  This is cheating.  They might as well make us uneasy by hiring people to inject drugs into our veins.  If Jack Valenti or someone were to ban the use of all non-musical noises that are neither part of nor representative of anything in the fictional world ... well, perhaps we'd lose a little something of value here and there (I gather that during the fight scenes in Raging Bull we hear bird screeches, for instance), but directors and composers would be forced to use their brains, and we'd all gain.P.S. It's both bizarre and disturbing when a film collects half a dozen attractive women just so that we can watch them get killed off, one by one, with perhaps one or two survivors ... so in a way it's kind of a relief that with one exception the actresses in Valentine are either stone-cold unattractive, or somehow made to look that way. Even low-budget studios knew there was a profit to be made and a few direct-to-video cheapies found there way on the market (CAMP BLOOD, PARTY CRASHER). But by 2001 the fad was starting to wear off and VALENTINE was the proof. A box office disappointment, it sounded the death toll for the late 90's/early 2000's slashers. (Warning contains spoilers!) One of them, Shelley, has just escaped from a droning Valentines date. Skipping off to the local morgue where she works, she is persistently stalked and killed by a mysterious prowler in a cupid mask. It's here where VALENTINE shines. The scenes of the cupid killer chasing Shelley through the corridors and stabbing and slashing through body bags in order to find the frightened girl, who is hiding in one of them, are pretty tense.
