It was not, however, until the seventies that the slasher movie began to emerge as a recognisable genre in its own right, with its own set of rules and conventions.The films to which Valentine is most indebted are probably the Halloween series, which started in 1978. Indeed, the name is probably an oblique reference to that series, All Hallows Eve and St Valentine's Day both being originally religious festivals which have taken on more secular connotations in recent years.The film is set around Valentine's day. (Or at least, it is supposedly so set. The outdoor scenes were obviously shot in the summer rather than in February). A group of young women receive sinister, threatening Valentine's cards, then one by one they are murdered in various gruesome ways by a mysterious stranger wearing a cupid mask. Apart from being friends, the one thing they have in common is that they were all at school together and that, about a decade or so earlier, they were all asked to dance at a school prom by the class nerd, an unattractive, unpopular boy named Jeremy. Four of them rudely rebuffed him, and the fifth falsely accused him of assaulting her, leading to his being beaten up and humiliated by a gang of bullies. It is presumed that Jeremy is the murderer and that his motive is revenge for his humiliation at the school dance. There is an attempt to provide a surprise ending, but this is so muddled and badly done that I ended up not knowing who the murderer actually was or what his- or her- motives were.The acting is uniformly poor, even though there are several relatively well-known faces in the cast- Bond girl Denise Richards, Katherine Heigl and David Boreanaz of Buffy fame. Heigl, whose character is the first to be killed, apparently signed up for the film without having read the full script, which would explain a lot. Richards's presence in this film provides evidence in support of the Curse of Bond theory- the theory which states that winning a part as a Bond girl will act as a permanent blight on the career of the actress concerned.Some recent slasher films, such as the Scream and Scary Movie franchises, have attempted to poke fun at the genre, but Valentine is a slasher movie of the semi-serious type rather than a deliberate parody. I say semi-serious because, whatever the intentions of the film-makers may have been, it is now virtually impossible to take any film in this genre seriously. There have been so many ludicrously bad examples that the genre has effectively parodied itself. There is a long list of well-worn conventions associated- the weird mask worn by the killer, the moralising tone whereby the victims all have some guilty secret, the terrified-girl-alone in-a-building-with-the-killer situation- all of which are religiously followed here. There appears to have been no attempt to make anything fresh or original. The result is a dull, formulaic, clichéd movie, an example of the slasher genre at its worst. It was billed as a thriller, but is about as thrilling as cold rice pudding. The one good thing that can be said about it is that it did not spawn a franchise of sequels. 2/10. And that's generous. "},{"Title":"Another Predictable, Run of the Chills Slasher with Little Wit","Date":"20 March 2008","Score":"1 out of 6 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" Urban Legend director Jamie Blanks takes another whack at the slasher movie genre with Valentine and stabs himself in the foot. His superficial but straightforward slice and dice saga about a demented lunatic who wears a shiny plastic Cupid's mask and slays a gaggle of gorgeous twentysomethings lacks originality, suspense, and charismatic characters. The scene aptly epitomizing Valentine occurs after a curvaceous cutie finds a heart shaped box of gift chocolates on her doorstep. When she bites into one of the rich, gooey pieces, she discovers to her horror that maggots are squirming around in it! Valentine doesn't get any better that this allusion to Dario Argento's classic Suspiria. Although the body count rises every quarter-hour with robotic monotony and the filmmakers spill enough blood for an R-rating, the comparatively generic murders capture little of the adrenaline edge required to set your heart to trip-hammering. Hardcore horror aficionados that relish the good stuff will feel cheated. Generally, Valentine recycles all the formulaic clichés and conventions of slasher from the 1970s & 1980s but sacrifices any sense of ingenuity and inspiration. Without the humor of the Scream trilogy or the gore of the Friday the 13th flicks, Valentine leaves a taste as yucky as a half-eaten maggot. Obviously, the people that made Valentine missed Scary Movie. The Wayans Brothers skewered virtually every murderous scene here so the whole movie suffers from a bad case of déjà vu! The action unfolds at Robert F. Kennedy Middle School during a sixth grade Valentine's Day dance. Eleven-year old Jeremy Melton, a naïve, goofy-toothed geek in heavy-framed spectacles, asks the prettiest girl to dance. Three turn him down rudely; one says 'maybe,' and Dorothy&#151;heftier than her haughty friends&#151;convinces Jeremy to make out with her beneath the bleachers. While they are necking, several bullies harass them. Mortified, Dorothy reels in alarm and accuses Jeremy of attacking her. The bullies drench Jeremy with red punch (similar to Brian De Palma's Carrie where Sissy Spacek got baptized in pig's blood) then strip him to his shorts and send him packing out of the gym. The trauma of this ordeal scars Jeremy so badly that his nose bleeds whenever he stresses out. His bleeding snout emerges as a recurring character trait that symbolizes the closure of each murder. Later, when our heroines confer with a cop in what amounts to an obvious bout of exposition, we learn that Jeremy went to reform school but wound up in an insane asylum. Eventually, we learn that Jeremy's parents died in a mysterious fire, and photos of Jeremy survived the blaze.Indeed, not only are Blanks and his scribes not content with making a slasher, but they also try to forge an Agatha Christie whodunit. They manage to assemble all the appropriate elements, but they have overlooked adding enough red herring to challenge audiences. No matter how many bathroom breaks or concession stand forays you make, you should have little difficulty in cracking this mediocre whodunit. The characters are so stupid that they never see the end coming, and the ending of Valentine is so contrived that even the surviving characters should have known better.Anyway, thirteen years elapse in a flash. All five dames have matured and embarked on either a career or college. Nobody gives poor Jeremy a second thought. Kate (Marley Shelton of Sugar & Spice, a sweetheart who struggles with alcoholic boyfriend Adam (David Boreanaz of TV's Buffy the Vampire Slayer), have become a journalist. Hard-to-get Paige (Denise Richards of Wild Things) admits in retrospect that they mistreated Jeremy. Medical school student Shelly (Katherine Heigl of 27 Dresses) has gone her own way to college. She prefers to dissect male cadavers rather than dine out with a real-live fellow. Slutty Lily (Jessica Cauffiel of White Chicks) still lets her hormones rule her and hangs out with Paige, while insecure rich girl Dorothy (Jessica Capshaw of Minority Report) takes advantage of her wealth and affluence to host big parties for her friends. Aside from Kate, none are remotely sympathetic despite their stunning looks. The girls haven't had any reason to stay in touch until the authorities discover Shelly's mutilated remains in the morgue of the university. Somehow, the Cupid killer gained access to the morgue and caught Shelly hiding in a body bag before he stabbed her repeatedly to death. Before long, the girls receive sicko Valentine Day cards with messages like Roses are red/ Violets are blue/They'll need dental records to identify you. Eventually, our masked menace in a Navy watch coat tracks them down and kills them with a vengeance that recognizes no restraint.Sadly, Valentine qualifies as a predictable, run-of-the-chills slasher. Consistently, the women behave like clueless cretins. They display the singular knack of isolating themselves in dark, dead-end places away from any source of help and get the axe. Typically, the slasher never breaks a sweat. He trudges along with the comatose gait of a zombie and always seems to get his guy or gal. Blanks competently stages the murders in a variety of creepy settings, and lenser Rick Bota's atmospheric, widescreen photography enhances the mood. Unfortunately, because the victims act so much like morons when the killer confronts them, you feel like you should cheer the villain instead of the heroines. Oddly enough, if anybody should win our sympathy, Jeremy should. After all, he was the one who was humiliated and whose life was destroyed. Nevertheless, Blanks blurs the morality when the heroines show what wenches they are. Apart from Kate, each shows herself in a negative light that alienates her from audience sympathy. Moreover, everything between the death scenes in Valentine generates little urgency. Far too much to the story relies on contrivances rather than character motivated movement.Altogether, Valentine qualifies as half-hearted hokum. As the killer strikes again the police race to find JM while the friends try to keep safe. From the very plot summary you can spot two things, 1) this is a very basic 'teen' slasher and 2) the plot is poor. Pre-conceptions perhaps but they are correct in this case as this is nothing but a genre flick and it is one that suffers from really poor writing. The plot starts and continues by making it totally clear who the killer is &#150; in fact so clear that only a fool would be taken in by it &#150; the phrase 'he doth protest too much' comes to mind when considering how hard this film tries to get us to accept that he is the killer. Despite this the film plods on and I suppose at least it is different from it throwing us red-herrings all the time but the eventual twist is all the more tiring for the fact that we know it must be coming. The film throws up quite graphic killings, not gory but quite vicious but the problem is they aren't scary &#150; they are just unpleasant and I'm not into that for its own sake (although some may be).The writing is uninspired as it is punctuated by murders every 10 minutes or so and the rest of the film is almost padding with poor dialogue. Compounding this problem is the fact that the characters are awful. The girls are all beautiful and really bad to all the men in their lives &#150; how was I supposed to care about a collection of rather preppy b*tches who are presented as quite air-headed! To excuse this behaviour the script makes all the men jerks and none of them have any character and only serve as red-herrings in the final 20 minutes. In one regard the casting of mostly b-grade actors makes it harder to guess who will live and who will die and I wasn't able to predict them. Richards is sexy but gives a poor 'air head slut' performance; Boreanaz is given almost nothing to do until the end (where he is used in a stupid way) and if you can't figure out why then you must be thick! The rest of the cast include Shelton, Capshaw, Cauffiel and Heigl who all run around and scream lots. None of them are any good but it is mostly because the material is so poor.Overall this is poor even by genre standards. The violent scenes are just nasty and are not tense or scary; the dialogue is terrible, the characters nonexistent and, when the twist inevitably comes is it stupid, illogical and a total insult to the intelligence of the audience. Even compared to other films that have the same genre weaknesses then this is poor &#150; no scares, no thrills, no characters, no plot, no logic and no point. A vacuous and stupid film. Sure it's banal modern day horror junk that hangs together by clichés and stupid plot holes, but at least it's never boring and it's actually quite funny in a cheesy kind of way. Five hot twenty-something babes, seemly with a lot of free time on their hands, all receive shocking Valentine cards signed with the initials J.M. Could this be the morbid revenge of a nerdy kid that the popular girls collectively humiliated during a school dance more than 12 years ago? The joke really becomes alarming when Shelly is found brutally murdered...and she's only number one. The poorly written script is (unintentionally?) hilarious! Even though it are mainly just girls that get slaughtered, this movie is very man-unfriendly! Every male character that gets introduced is either a sexual pervert or a socially dysfunctional loser...most are even both! Heck, even the police inspector turns out to be an obscene freak! There's absolutely no tension and you can predict every next twist hours in advance. The beauty-queen killings are reasonably inventive but almost entirely bloodless, so gore-hounds beware. The ending (as in the actual revelation of the killer's identity) is totally absurd and makes the movie even worse that Jamie Blanks' previous turkey Urban Legend. In fact, Valentine was released 20 years too late! With a plot and gore opportunities like this, it could have been a minor 80's slasher-classic like Happy Birthday To Me or &#150; oh yes &#150; My Bloody Valentine. Nobody cares about such slashers anymore nowadays. The politically correct American horror standards don't allow nudity or brutal gore and that's why every new slasher attempt looks lame. Pretty good teen slasher.","Date":"2 September 2005","Score":"1 out of 16 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" Valentine starts with Jeremy Melton (Joel Palmer) the school nerd being rejected & publicly humiliated by every half decent looking female at a school valentine party, that is until he comes across the equally desperate & fat Dorothy Wheeler (Kate Logie) whom at fist is eager to get it on with Jeremy but then decides to humiliate him even more when everyone else catches them together by saying that Jeremy attacked her... It's now '13 Years Later', Valentine's Day is fast approaching & the girls from that night all those years ago are looking for love including med student Shelly Fisher (Katherine Heigl) who has just had a nightmare date with a dork named Jason Marquette (Adam Harrington). Shortly after Shelly receives a threatening Valentine's card & is brutally murdered. Four of Shelly's close friends from school, the fat Dorothy (Jessica Capshaw), the popular Kate Davies (Marley Shelton, the funny Lily Voight (Jessica Cauffiel) & the very sexy Paige Prescott (Denise Richards) attend the funeral where Detective Vaughn (Fulvio Cecere) tells them to be careful. Which turns out to be good advice as strange things start to happen, more creepy Valentine cards, chocolates with live maggots inside, clothes being taken & the small matter of a psycho murderer in a cherub mask who has his sights set on revenge...This American Australian co-production was directed by Jamie Blanks & is a pretty good entry into the popular slasher film sub genre started by the likes of Halloween (1978) & Friday the 13th (1980). The script by Donna Powers, Wayne Powers, Gretchen J. Berg & Aaron Harberts based on the novel by Tom Savage moves along at a nice pace, it has a nice mystery angle to it with plenty of suspects & red herrings as to whom the killer may be. The characters are quite likable for the most part & unusually for an almost entire teen cast nobody got on my nerves. Valentine is far from original as this has nothing new to offer slasher fans than any of the similarly themed films from 25 years ago. It uses the clichés & stereotypes well enough to create a film in it's own right & I found myself rather liking it. On the negative side the Valentine angle could have been used more other than a couple of cards with threatening messages written on them & the killing methods could have been Valentine or love themed like Lily's death when she is shot by arrows which is obviously a cupid inspired murder, the ending seems to confuse a lot of people as well although I think it's quite clever & very satisfying. Valentine could have used some more gore & deaths, according to the IMDb's 'Altenate Versions' section Warner Bros. made director Blanks edit the film for violence which annoys the hell out of me & it even suggests that the murder of Dorthy's stepmother was cut completely, damn studios. Valentine has good set pieces including a murder committed in a maze of monitors at an art show, the opening in a morgue & when Paige is killed in a Jacuzzi with a huge drill. It has that slasher feel to it & is very well made with nice cinematography & production design considering it's budget of about $10,000,000. The gore & violence is disappointingly tame, an off screen slit throat (one scene that was cut apparently), someone is shot with arrows, someone has their throat impaled on broken glass, an axe in someone's back & a scene involving a drill. The cast all put in decent performances & all look gorgeous apart from Jessica Capshaw who has a square jaw & just looks strange if you stare at her for too long. A special mention goes to Denise Richards who is a total babe & we get to see her in a very skimpy swimming outfit which is almost worth the price of a rental on it's own. David Boreanaz better known as Angel (1999 - 2004) makes an appearance & does an OK job. I liked Valentine, I thought it was a fine slasher film for modern audiences. Definitely worth a watch if not just for Denise Richards... You would think in the wake of movies like Scream filmmakers would try something new. Sadly not. The plot is old (this has been done hundreds of times--a masked killer stalking women--how original!), it's suspenseless and the acting--wellllllll. David Boreanaz is very good as an ex of one of the girls, but he's wasted in a minor role. Everyone else is bad--and I mean EVERYONE! Even Denise Richards (who can be amusing) sucks. The worst thing about this movie is that it's too timid. There's no nudity (even though there are plenty of chances) and the murders are very tame--a little blood and that's about it. If you're going to do a stupid slasher film at least give us gore! Also logic disappears frequently (one woman running from the killer has two choices...a door leading outside, one leading to a sauna. Guess which one she picks? The sauna!!!!), and the ending is screamingly obvious. It's an insult to horror fans (like myself) and everybody else will be bored. You end up rooting for the killer! Avoid at all costs! "},{"Title":"Awful Slasher","Date":"2 December 2008","Score":"0 out of 22 people found the following review useful","Genre":"Horror, Thriller","Review":" Valentine (2001)* (out of 4) Four girls are being stalked by Cupid and they seem to think the guy might be a loser from middle school who they all picked on.
